Today, 75 years later, the story of Tony and the 10 Americans is being remembered. The @royalairforce alongside the @usairforce completed a fly past to honour their sacrifice and Tonyâ€™s dedication. #RememberTheTen https://t.co/ffzuEB9zAl
In 1969 a plaque was built for the 10 Americans that gave their lives for the young Britons. For decades Tony has visited it. He lays his hand on the memorial as he talks about small things. His plans for the day, the weather. He never stopped trying to keep their memories alive.
Pilot Kriegshauser made a choice. Instead of risking the lives of Tony &amp; the other children, he steered the plane into the trees just beyond the park as the last engine failed. The plane crashed. There were no survivors. But Tony would never forget that moment as long as he lived
There were 10 Americans aboard the B-17 Flying Fortress â€œMi Amigoâ€. Sputtering, the plane was returning from a harrowing WWII mission over Berlin when an engine failed. 23 year old Pilot Kriegshauser steered the B-17 to a park to crash land. It was then that he saw the children.
In Sheffield 1944, 8 year old Tony Foulds &amp; his friends were playing outside when they heard a loud roar. Tony looked up to see a plane so low he could see the pilot waving at him. Tony waved back. It was only later he would realise the pilot was trying to get him out of the way. https://t.co/k1ZNtrqEx0

This week British scientists will be in DC for @AAASmeetings where many women will be recognised for their work in science, including prolific British science communicator Joanna Verran, who has been awarded the 2019 AAAS Award for Public Engagement: https://t.co/fsgM1MGBUG
One of the many inspiring British scientists of today, Maggie Aderin-Pocock is a space scientist &amp; science educator. A co-presenter of the astronomy TV programme @BBCStargazing, she continuously works toward promoting the study of science among young girls. https://t.co/cjcF7SW8JC
Jocelyn Burnell is an astrophysicist from N.Ireland. As a research assistant @Cambridge_Uni in 1967 she co-discovered radio pulsars. Her male advisor was awarded a Nobel for the finding in 1974. In 2018 Burnell donated a $3m prize to support women, minority &amp; refugee students. https://t.co/OLofoNKspd
61 years after her death, Rosalind's search for the building blocks of life will continue...on the surface of Mars! Last week @spacegovuk announced that the new @ESA_Exomars' rover will be named after Rosalind Franklin. https://t.co/E5vLbKhjy4
Rosalind Franklin defied expectations her entire life. Though her father didnt approve of women in higher education, she earned a PhD in physical chemistry from @Cambridge_Uni in 1945 &amp; despite gender discrimination, she broke ground in her invaluable X-ray crystallography of DNA https://t.co/htsu54Q3ki
Kathleen E. Carpenter was a champion of Welsh ecology. During the 1920s, she received MSc &amp; PhD degrees from @AberUni and in the years that followed, she wrote the first British textbook on freshwater ecology, titled Life In Inland Waters. https://t.co/2ursVg9urw
Isabella Gordon was born in Scotland in 1901. She was a zoologist who specialized in studying crabs &amp; sea spiders, obtaining a PhD in 1926 &amp; spending most of her career w/ @NHM_London. She was highly respected in museum &amp; research communities &amp; receive an OBE in 1963. https://t.co/aBnny51Pkj
Mary Pickford was born in India in 1902 and raised in the UK. She was a pioneer neuroendocrinologist, one of the first woman to be elected to the @BritPharmSoc, &amp; the first woman appointed to a medical professorship at @EdinburghUni. https://t.co/0mKADjduQL
Elizabeth Blackwell was a British physician. When she applied to med school, male students voted to admit her as a joke. She graduated at the top of her class in 1849, becoming the 1st woman in the US to earn an M.D. She went on to open her own medical school for women. https://t.co/7VPDzQEzeQ
Mary Anning was born in poverty in 1799. Though many scientists of the day insisted a woman of such a deprived background couldnt posses the knowledge &amp; skills she displayed, Mary became a self-taught paleontologist, her fossil discoveries including plesiosaur &amp; pterosaur fossils https://t.co/Vd90AtyQ7X

Leefe Robinson received the quickest Victoria Cross ever awarded in 1916 for taking down a German airship over Britain but was later captured by the Germans. Though he was released in 1918, Robinson died from influenza. Thousands of mourners came to his funeral. Â© IWM (Q 66470) https://t.co/q7dkh5Q3da
Jack Cornwell joined the @RoyalNavy when he was 15. Cornwell served during the Battle of Jutland. When the battle was over, medics arrived to find Jack awaiting orders despite being mortally wounded. He later died from his injuries. He was 16. https://t.co/k0drPvDYPk
Albert Ball volunteered with the Royal Flying Corps. On 7 May 1917 after his 44th victory Ball's plane was shot down. He received a posthumous Victoria Cross presented to his family by King George V. https://t.co/XnrMBwKsCR
Indra Lal Roy served with the Royal Flying Corps. Within 13 days of flying he achieved 10 victories including 3 in just 4 hours. Tragically, the day of his final victory in 1918 he was shot down at the age of 19. He is recognized as the 1st &amp; only Indian flying ace of WWI. https://t.co/GSZ4hN9QS5
Edith Cavell was a nurse behind enemy lines in Belgium during the War. She helped smuggle 200 British, French &amp; Belgian soldiers out of Belgium before she was arrested &amp; executed by firing squad in 1915. The story of her courage was heard around the world. Â© IWM (Q 32930) https://t.co/oV8sJS4dHf

Tirpitz was a pig originally aboard a German cruiser that sank in March 1915. Tirpitz escaped the wreck. She was spotted by the crew of HMS Glasgow &amp; saved by a member of the crew. The ship made Tirpitz their mascot until 1916 when she was retired near Portsmouth. https://t.co/9mh3gBDR8w

Oct 2017: VPNFILTER malware infected 1000s of home &amp; small business routers &amp; network devices worldwide. The infection potentially allowed attackers to control infected devices, render them inoperable &amp; intercept or block network traffic.
The UK government attributed this attack to the GRU in Feb 2018. @NCSC assess with high confidence that the GRU was almost certainly responsible. https://t.co/TIffCT7Ku6
June 2017: A destructive cyber attack targeted the Ukrainian financial, energy &amp; gov sectors but spread further affecting other European &amp; Russian businesses.
Oct 2017: BadRabbit ransomware encrypted hard drives &amp; rendered  IT inoperable. This caused disruption including to the Kyiv metro, Odessa airport, Russiaâ€™s central bank &amp; two Russian media outlets.		@NCSC assess w/ high confidence that the GRU was almost certainly responsible.

More information about The Duchess's Coat of Arms: https://t.co/nTrAhSozrI
Her Royal Highness worked closely with the College of Arms throughout the design process to create a Coat of Arms that was both personal and  representative.
The three quills represent communication and the power of words. Beneath the shield on the grass sits a collection of golden poppies, California's state flower, and wintersweet, which grows at Kensington Palace.
The blue background of the shield represents the Pacific Ocean off the  California coast, while the two golden rays across the shield are symbolic of the sunshine of The Duchess's home state.
